URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS154299276	2017-05-15 17:30:19	18377	species	Cassin's Vireo	Vireo cassinii			2				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Clark	US-NV-003		33	USFWS_591		Desert NWR--Corn Creek (Field Station)	L168656	H	36.4387970	-115.3595660	2012-05-05	05:30:00	obsr235247	S10838974	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	420	3.219		2	1		0	1	0		Experienced an absolutely amazing migrant fallout on 5/5 at Corn Creek just north of Las Vegas.  David Donsker and I arrived at Corn Creek at first light and immediately noticed a number of kingbirds flying into the trees from the desert.  As the steady stream of birds continued, we noticed numerous warblers flying in along with the kingbirds.  The first tree we reached was loaded with Western Kingbirds, although only 10 feet tall it had at least 50 kingbirds on it perched like Christmas tree ornaments.  Each binocular field in each mulberry tree contained at least 5 Bullock's Orioles and a few more Western Kingbirds.  Groups of 5 to 10 warblers (mostly Audubon's) were in the trees, on the ground, in the grass, on fence posts - just everywhere.  We birded the oasis from 5:15 to 11 and conservatively estimated 2,000 birds of 75 species.  Counting was next to impossible as the birds were constantly flitting from tree to tree.  We returned and birded the area again from 2:30 to 5:30, and although activity was much lower, there were still hundreds of migrants, several more still flying in from the desert, and we found several species we didn't have in the morning.   Also saw 1 hybrid Eur Collared-Dove X Mourning Dove but could not determine how to enter this into e-bird.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS56293060	2017-04-18 17:05:33	18377	species	Cassin's Vireo	Vireo cassinii			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Nye	US-NV-023	US-NV_977	33	USFWS_350		Ash Meadows NWR HQ	L388900	H	36.4204294	-116.3299853	1965-04-14	06:15:00	obsr56422	S4058241	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	405	4.023	4.0469	2	1		0	1	0		Potash Springs, Longstreet Springs, Frog Springs and Rodgers Springs. Habitat varies, see bird notes. 55F, warm, sunny. This is a Desert Ecology Class, Chico State College. We are in the northern end of Ash Meadows in western Nevada. It is a hot, arid land with steep rising mountains which almost totally lack any type of vegetation. Potash Springs, one mile north of Longstreet Springs was where we camped. The springs are an oasis in the desert. Vegetation is very sparse and located primarily around these springs. Plants are Tamarisk, willow, cottonwood,  and some sedges. Away from water the basic shrubs are Mesquite. Some succulents and Creosote present. Buildings at the various sights were built around 1860. Potash Springs is approx. 4 miles west of SR29 and about 10 miles south of Lathrop Wells, NV. Frog Springs and Rodger Springs are located inbetween Potash and Longstreet Springs.----Observers: Myself and Dr. Dempsey----Footnote: 8PM, Lou Davis and I went north 19 miles to some sand dunes. Only insect present were 3 beetles, some grubs and 5 Dune Crickets. These crickets never before found this far north. All beetles proceeding up dunes, none down. When sand was pushed down, beetles always remained on top or ahead of moving sand. 10PM	Longstreet Springs. Desert: Oasis/Alkali

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS22371209	2018-11-28 14:50:13	18377	species	Cassin's Vireo	Vireo cassinii			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Washoe	US-NV-031	US-NV_2211	15			Lower Marlette Creek area (Washoe Co.; Marlette Lake Trail below the switchbacks)	L866938	H	39.1678344	-119.9265701	2004-07-10	04:00:00	obsr16674	S1693546	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	210	4.828		2	1	G189367	0	1	0		John Anderson called me Friday night to discuss plans for a July big day that we had talked about earlier.  We iterated through the state checklist and discussed where the best place to find each bird would be.  I wrote down some species that I had no idea where to find (where does one see Violet-green Swallows in July near Reno?) and planned to do some research and scouting.  "So, when do you want to go?" I asked.  "Is tomorrow OK?", John replied.  So much for planning, but I immediately agreed to have him pick me up at 3:00 AM to head to Lake Tahoe.  On to the birds:----Our general strategy was to pick up mountain birds in the morning, shorebirds and waterbirds in the afternoon, and riparian sage birds in the evening.  We had a difficult time leaving the spectacle of shorebirds at Carson Lake, so our riparian birds were duly neglected. Big misses include Bullock's Oriole, Tree Swallow, House Wren, Townsend's Solitaire, Bushtit,Brewer's Sparrow and Red-breasted Sapsucker.  Not-so-big misses include Blue Grouse, Canyon Wren, Rock Wren, Pinyon Jay, Wood Duck, Black-throated Sparrow, Violet-green Swallow, and Sage Sparrow.  Unexpected surprises included a calling SAW-WHET OWL at Chimney Beach, 20 high-flying WHITE PELICANS over Mt. Rose Meadows, 2 HOODED MERGANSERS at Virginia Lake, and a pair of breeding-plumage COMMON LOONS(!!) on Big Soda Lake in Fallon.

Generally a contrasty bird with green back, darker grey head and yellow flanks, but perhaps not as distinct as would be expected for a Blue-headed. Hypothetically it could have been a western race Blue-headed, but I didn't see it well enough for this and the song sounded slightly too burry for a Blue-headed, though slightly clearer than some Cassin's. Apparently bright individuals are expected in fall for vireos (per Don Roberson) so it makes me wonder about the supposed bright bird I saw in May once...
